We first see\n261:   // if the stream needs to be reset. If it needs to be, this will end up invoking reset callbacks\n262:   // and then moving the stream to the deferred destruction list. If the stream has not been reset,\n263:   // we move it to the deferred deletion list here. Then, we potentially close the connection. This\n264:   // must be done after deleting the stream since the stream refers to the connection and must be\n265:   // deleted first.\n266:   bool reset_stream = false;\n267:   // If the response encoder is still associated with the stream, reset the stream. If there are many streams\n715:   // that may result in a stack overflow. This flag is used to avoid above recursion.\n716:   if (drained_due_to_premature_resets_) {\n717:     return;\n718:   }\n719: \n720:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ == 0) {\n721:     return;\n722:   }\n723: \n724:   const uint64_t limit =\n725:       runtime_.snapshot().getInteger(ConnectionManagerImpl::PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey, 500);\n726: \n727:   if (closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_ < limit) {\n728:     // Even though the total number of streams have not reached `limit`, check if the number of bad\n729:     // streams is high enough that even if every subsequent stream is good, the connection\n730:     // would be closed once the limit is reached, and if so close the connection now.\n731:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < limit) {\n732:       return;\n733:     }\n734:   } else {\n735:     if (number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 < closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_) {\n736:       return;\n737:     }\n738:   }\n739: \n740:   if (read_callbacks_->connection().state() == Network::Connection::State::Open) {\n741:     stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_.inc();\n742: \n743:     // Mark the the connection has been drained due to too many premature resets.\n744:     drained_due_to_premature_resets_ = true;\n745: \n746:     doConnectionClose(Network::ConnectionCloseType::Abort, absl::nullopt,\n747:                       \"too_many_premature_resets\");\n748:   }\n749: }\n750: \n751: void ConnectionManagerImpl::onGoAway(GoAwayErrorCode) {\n752:   // Currently we do nothing with remote go away frames. void ConnectionManagerImpl::ActiveStream::maybeRecordLastByteReceived(bool end_stream) {\n1303:   // If recreateStream is called, the HCM rewinds state and may send more encodeData calls.\n1304:   if complicated, but important.\n1312: //\n1313: // We want to do minimal work before selecting route and creating a filter\n1314: // chain to maximize the number of requests which get custom filter behavior,\n1315: // e.g. registering access logging.\n1316: //\n1317: // This must be balanced by doing sanity checking for invalid requests (one\n1318: // can't route select properly without full headers), checking state required to\n1319: // serve error responses (connection close, head requests, etc), and\n1320: // modifications which may themselves affect route selection.\n1321: void While the existing test suite covers main request/response flows and basic error handling, several critical code paths remain untested or partially tested. The identified gaps primarily involve edge cases in error handling, state machine transitions, and resource management under complex scenarios. These gaps could allow subtle bugs related to resource leaks, state corruption, and incorrect error propagation to reach production.\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Codec Creation Failure Under Overload with Partial State\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 507-515\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The `onData()` method checks for overload before creating the codec (lines 509-512) and calls `handleCodecOverloadError()` if shedding load. However, the code does not test the specific scenario where codec creation begins but partially fails after some initialization (e.g., buffer allocation succeeds but codec instantiation fails). The current test suite exercises the success path and the overload rejection path, but not the partial failure scenario. If codec creation leaves objects in an inconsistent state, subsequent calls to `onData()` may behave unpredictably.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `CodecCreationPartialFailureRecovery`\n  - Setup: Mock `config_->createCodec()` to succeed on first call partially (allocate internal buffers), then fail on re-entry\n  - Action: Call `onData()` with valid HTTP data\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify connection is properly cleaned up (no dangling codec pointers)\n    - Verify stats are correctly incremented (codec_creation_error counter)\n    - Verify subsequent `onData()` calls don't crash or leak resources\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  A partially initialized codec could lead to memory leaks, nullptr dereferences, or double-free bugs. This is especially critical in production systems handling thousands of concurrent connections under load.\n\n### Gap 2: Premature Reset Detection Heuristic Edge Cases\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 702-749 (function `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()`)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  The premature reset detection uses a heuristic formula (`number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2`) to decide whether to drain the connection (lines 731, 735). The test suite does not cover:\n  - Boundary conditions where `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2` exactly equals the limit\n  - Overflow scenarios when `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` is very large (near UINT64_MAX)\n  - Rapid successive premature resets in a single dispatch cycle\n  - Interaction with the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag preventing recursion (the flag itself is well-tested, but the boundary conditions triggering it are not)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `PrematureResetEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Set `number_premature_stream_resets_` = 250 and `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` = 500 (exactly at 2x boundary). Verify connection is drained.\n  - Test Case 2: Set `number_premature_stream_resets_` = 249 and `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` = 500 (just below boundary). Verify connection is NOT drained.\n  - Test Case 3: Create 1000 streams, reset 60% prematurely in rapid succession. Verify GOAWAY is sent exactly once, not multiple times.\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` is incremented exactly once\n    - Verify `doConnectionClose()` is called exactly once\n    - Verify subsequent `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` calls are no-ops due to `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Premature resets often indicate a client or network problem. Failing to detect and isolate such connections could allow malicious clients to degrade service for other users. Conversely, false positives (draining connections that shouldn't be drained) could reduce availability.\n\n### Gap 3: Header Validation and Transformation Error Path Coverage\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 1195-1254 (function `validateHeaders()` including transformation)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The header validation logic handles multiple failure scenarios:\n  - Path normalization redirects (line 1210-1227: sets Location header, responds with 307)\n  - gRPC special handling (line 1228-1230: uses grpc_status instead of response_code)\n  - HTTP/2 underscore validation special case (line 1238-1247: resets stream instead of sending response)\n\n  Current tests focus on the happy path and basic validation failure. The test suite does NOT cover:\n  - Interaction between multiple validation failures (e.g., underscore violation AND path normalization redirect)\n  - gRPC stream responses to header validation failures (does gRPC-specific error handling work correctly?)\n  - Edge case where `response_encoder_->streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` returns different values per stream\n  - Validation of trailers (separate function `validateTrailers()` at lines 1256-1300) with edge cases like trailers containing underscores\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `HeaderValidationEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Send request with invalid underscore AND attempt path normalization. Verify HTTP/2 codec resets stream (not sending 400).\n  - Test Case 2: Send gRPC request with invalid Content-Type header. Verify response code is Internal (grpc_status) not BadRequest.\n  - Test Case 3: Send trailers with underscores on HTTP/1. Verify local reply is sent (not stream reset).\n  - Test Case 4: Send trailers with invalid encoding on HTTP/2. Verify codec error is NOT triggered (per line 1295 check).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify correct response codes (307, 400, or stream reset) based on protocol and error type\n    - Verify gRPC status codes are set when appropriate\n    - Verify stats are correct (`downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_`, `downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path_`)\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Invalid header handling is the first line of defense against protocol violations. Bugs here could allow malformed requests to bypass validation, reach upstream services, or cause protocol state corruption in HTTP/2 and HTTP/3.\n\n### Gap 4: Filter Chain Continuation with 1xx Headers Interaction\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/filter_manager.cc\n- **Lines**: 61-146 (function `ActiveStreamFilterBase::commonContinue()`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The filter continuation logic is complex when 1xx (informational) headers are involved. Lines 88-96 show:\n  ```cpp\n  if (has1xxHeaders()) {\n    continued_1xx_headers_ = true;\n    do1xxHeaders();\n    if (!parent_.filter_manager_callbacks_.responseHeaders()) {\n      return;  // Early exit if final headers not yet arrived\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n\n  Current tests verify basic 1xx header flow, but NOT:\n  - What happens if a filter modifies `continued_1xx_headers_` state during `do1xxHeaders()` (should be impossible but not explicitly asserted)\n  - If `has1xxHeaders()` returns true but `do1xxHeaders()` somehow fails to actually send them\n  - If both `has1xxHeaders()` and `hasTrailers()` return true - which takes priority in continuation order?\n  - If response headers arrive WHILE `do1xxHeaders()` is executing (re-entrancy with mixed state)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `FilterContinuation1xxInteraction`\n  - Test Case 1: Filter returns StopAllBuffer on first headers, then continues after 1xx headers received. Verify `do1xxHeaders()` is called before `doHeaders()`.\n  - Test Case 2: Multiple 1xx headers received (100 Continue, then 103 Early Hints). Verify both are processed, or verify behavior is well-defined for multiple 1xx headers.\n  - Test Case 3: 1xx headers received, then trailers received before continuation. Verify continuation order is: 1xx → headers → trailers.\n  - Test Case 4: Filter returns `StopAllWatermark`, then watermark is resolved while 1xx headers are pending. Verify 1xx headers are still processed.\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `do1xxHeaders()` and `doHeaders()` are called in correct order\n    - Verify `doTrailers()` is called after headers, not before\n    - Verify stream state machine is consistent (no double-processing of headers)\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  HTTP/1.1 continues (100 Continue) and HTTP/1.1 early hints (103 Early Hints) require precise timing. Filter bugs could cause timeouts (client waits for 100 Continue), connection hangs, or protocol violations (sending headers twice).\n\n### Gap 5: HTTP/1 Soft Drain on Max Connection Duration\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 769-788 (function `onConnectionDurationTimeout()`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  When `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` is enabled for HTTP/1, the code avoids full drain sequence and instead sets `soft_drain_http1_ = true` (line 783). This is an optimization to avoid expensive GOAWAY for HTTP/1. However, the test suite does not cover:\n  - What happens if a NEW stream is created AFTER soft_drain_http1_ is set (line 437-441 in newStream() marks stream to drain on completion)\n  - Interaction between soft_drain and other drain sequences (what if startDrainSequence() was already called?)\n  - Verify that `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` is decremented exactly once in destructor (line 238)\n  - Edge case: soft_drain_http1_ set, then immediately another timeout fires (stream timeout, connection close timeout)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `HTTP1SoftDrainEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Set `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` = true, max_connection_duration = 100ms. Create a stream that takes longer than 100ms to complete. Verify `soft_drain_http1_` is set, stream still completes, then connection closes gracefully.\n  - Test Case 2: Multiple streams exist, max connection duration timeout fires. Verify all streams are allowed to complete (not forcibly closed like in full drain).\n  - Test Case 3: Soft drain timeout, then client sends another request. Verify request is accepted and processed (no immediate GOAWAY).\n  - Test Case 4: Soft drain flag set, then `onDrainTimeout()` is called. Verify GOAWAY is still sent (drain sequence takes precedence).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `soft_drain_http1_` flag is set (not starting full drain sequence)\n    - Verify `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` is incremented and later decremented\n    - Verify connection doesn't close until all streams complete\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Soft drain is a performance optimization to avoid expensive GOAWAY messages in HTTP/1. Bugs could cause unnecessary connection closures (impacting client performance) or violate the optimization contract (sending expensive GOAWAY anyway).\n\n### Gap 6: Stream End with Concurrent Trailers and End-Stream Events\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 259-310 (function `doEndStream()`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The `doEndStream()` function handles a complex scenario: deciding whether to reset the stream or let it complete naturally. Lines 271-273 check:\n  ```cpp\n  if (stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr &&\n      (!stream.filter_manager_.hasLastDownstreamByteReceived() ||\n       !stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_))\n  ```\n\n  The test suite covers basic stream end, but NOT:\n  - Stream end when trailers are present (hasTrailers() = true) but response_encoder is still attached\n  - The interaction between `hasLastDownstreamByteReceived()` and trailers (trailers should mark this as true, but are they processed before doEndStream()?)\n  - Call to `recreateStream()` which nulls out response_encoder (line 268 comment) - what if recreateStream() fails?\n  - Edge case where `state_.codec_saw_local_complete_` is true but request data is still being transmitted upstream\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `StreamEndWithTrailersEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Request with headers + trailers, filter takes a long time to process. Verify trailers are recorded via `maybeRecordLastByteReceived()` before stream end.\n  - Test Case 2: Response sent (marking local complete), then trailers arrive from downstream. Verify stream is reset (not allowed per HTTP semantics).\n  - Test Case 3: `recreateStream()` is called internally. Verify `response_encoder_` is properly nulled and stream is not reset.\n  - Test Case 4: Stream has trailers, doEndStream() is called, then filter injects more trailers. Verify order of operations (stream doesn't actually end mid-trailer-injection).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify trailers are properly recorded with timing information\n    - Verify stream reset happens when appropriate (incomplete requests)\n    - Verify response_encoder is not accessed after recreateStream()\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Stream end logic is critical for proper request lifecycle. Bugs could cause premature stream resets (losing data), protocol violations (sending response twice), or memory safety issues (use-after-free).\n\n### Gap 7: Request Header Timeout Firing During Filter Processing\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 1335-1338 (request_header_timer setup and disabling in decodeHeaders)\n- **Risk**: LOW\n- **Description**:\n  Request header timeout is set when a stream is created and disabled when headers are decoded (line 1336). However, the test suite does not cover:\n  - What if header timeout fires WHILE `decodeHeaders()` is executing? (Re-entrancy: timeout callback fires during header processing)\n  - What if timeout fires after headers received but before timeout is disabled? (Race condition)\n  - What if multiple streams are created and only some get their header timeouts fire?\n  - Interaction with stream-idle-timeout: which takes precedence if both fire simultaneously?\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `RequestHeaderTimeoutEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Create stream, immediately fire request_header_timer. Verify stream is reset (or connection is closed) before headers are processed.\n  - Test Case 2: Create stream, start sending headers but very slowly. Fire timeout during header transmission. Verify timeout is honored (not waiting for full headers).\n  - Test Case 3: Create two streams. Timeout fires on first stream while second stream is being created. Verify only first stream is affected.\n  - Test Case 4: Request headers timeout = 100ms, stream idle timeout = 200ms. Timeout fires at 100ms. Verify header timeout is enforced (not waiting for stream idle timeout).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_pending_header_timeout_` is incremented\n    - Verify connection is either closed or stream is reset\n    - Verify no leaked resources (timers, streams)\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Header timeouts protect against slowloris attacks. Missing edge case handling could allow attacks to slip through or cause false positives (legitimate slow clients).\n\n### Gap 8: Header Map Lazy-to-Eager Conversion Boundary Conditions\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 56-68 (function `HeaderMapImpl::HeaderList::maybeMakeMap()`)\n- **Risk**: LOW\n- **Description**:\n  The header map uses a lazy-map optimization. Headers are stored in a linked list until 3 headers are present, then a map is created (line 26: `kMinHeadersForLazyMap = 3`). The test suite covers basic operations, but NOT:\n  - Creating exactly 3 headers then immediately looking up a header (boundary condition triggering lazy map creation)\n  - Removing headers back to 2, then adding one more (does lazy map stay, or is it destroyed?)\n  - Performance characteristics: does the lazy map handle worst-case lookups efficiently?\n  - Header removal during map iteration (concurrent modification)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `HeaderMapLazyToEagerBoundary`\n  - Test Case 1: Add 2 headers, verify lazy_map is empty. Add 3rd header, verify lazy_map is created and contains all 3.\n  - Test Case 2: Add 3 headers (lazy map created), remove 1 header. Verify lazy map is correctly updated (not left in inconsistent state).\n  - Test Case 3: Add 5 headers (lazy map created), look up each via key. Verify all are found (lazy map is correct).\n  - Test Case 4: Add 10 custom headers with same name. Verify lazy map stores list of values correctly.\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify lazy_map_.empty() == true when headers.size() < 3\n    - Verify lazy_map_.empty() == false when headers.size() >= 3 (after first lazy_map trigger)\n    - Verify all lookups return correct values, whether lazy map is used or not\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Header map is used in the hot path for every HTTP request. Performance bugs or correctness issues here could cause O(n) behavior when O(log n) is expected, leading to CPU overhead or incorrect header values being returned.\n\n### Gap 9: Codec Error Propagation to Active Streams\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 463-482 (functions `handleCodecError()` and `handleCodecOverloadError()`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  When a codec error occurs (e.g., invalid frame format, protocol violation), `handleCodecError()` is called (line 529, 531, etc.). This function:\n  1. Sets response flag on the CONNECTION (line 466)\n  2. Calls `doConnectionClose()` (line 470)\n  3. Does NOT explicitly reset active streams\n\n  The assumption is that `doConnectionClose()` will handle stream cleanup. However, the test suite does not verify:\n  - What if `doConnectionClose()` is a no-op (e.g., connection already closed)? Do active streams leak?\n  - If a stream is in the middle of encoding a response when codec error occurs, is it properly reset?\n  - If codec error contains a non-ASCII error message (e.g., binary data), does response_details handle it correctly?\n  - What if multiple codec errors occur in rapid succession (e.g., due to buffer overflow)? Is doConnectionClose() called multiple times?\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `CodecErrorPropagation`\n  - Test Case 1: Create stream, start encoding response, then trigger codec protocol error (malformed frame). Verify stream is reset.\n  - Test Case 2: Create multiple streams, trigger codec error. Verify ALL streams are reset (not just the first one).\n  - Test Case 3: Codec error with invalid UTF-8 in error message. Verify error message is sanitized before use.\n  - Test Case 4: Codec error, then immediately another codec error. Verify doConnectionClose() is called once (not twice).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_protocol_error_` is incremented\n    - Verify all active streams call `onResetStream()` or similar cleanup\n    - Verify connection is closed with appropriate reason code\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Codec errors indicate protocol violations or malformed input. Proper handling ensures that malicious input doesn't cause resource leaks or leave the system in an inconsistent state. Bad actors could exploit gaps to cause denial of service or connection pool exhaustion.\n\n### Gap 10: Stream Creation with Buffer Account Memory Pressure\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 409-421 (buffer account creation in `newStream()`)\n- **Risk**: LOW\n- **Description**:\n  When a new stream is created, a buffer account is created for watermark tracking (lines 415-417). The test suite does NOT cover:\n  - What if buffer account creation fails (returns nullptr)? Does the code fall back gracefully?\n  - What if account creation succeeds but `setAccount()` fails?\n  - Memory pressure: if buffer factory is under memory pressure, does account creation return a degraded account? Is that handled?\n  - Multiple streams created under memory pressure: does each stream get a separate account, or do they share?\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `BufferAccountCreationEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Mock buffer factory to return null account. Verify stream is still created (uses default account).\n  - Test Case 2: Create stream when buffer tracking is disabled (account = nullptr). Verify stream creation succeeds without crashes.\n  - Test Case 3: Mock buffer factory to return a \"capped\" account (limited to 1KB). Create stream with large request. Verify watermarks are triggered.\n  - Test Case 4: Create 1000 streams with small buffer limits. Verify connection handles watermarks correctly (doesn't drop legitimate streams).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify stream is created even if account creation fails\n    - Verify watermark callbacks are registered correctly\n    - Verify no nullptr dereferences or segfaults\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Buffer watermarking is critical for backpressure handling. Bugs here could cause connections to hang (watermarks not triggered), leak memory (accounts not cleaned up), or miss legitimate requests (overly aggressive watermarking).\n\n## File References\n\nKey files analyzed in this coverage gap analysis:\n\n1. **source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc** — Core HCM implementation (1800+ lines)\n   - While the existing test suite covers main request/response flows and basic error handling, several critical code paths remain untested or partially tested. The identified gaps primarily involve edge cases in error handling, state machine transitions, and resource management under complex scenarios. These gaps could allow subtle bugs related to resource leaks, state corruption, and incorrect error propagation to reach production.\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Codec Creation Failure Under Overload with Partial State\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 507-515\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The `onData()` method checks for overload before creating the codec (lines 509-512) and calls `handleCodecOverloadError()` if shedding load. However, the code does not test the specific scenario where codec creation begins but partially fails after some initialization (e.g., buffer allocation succeeds but codec instantiation fails). The current test suite exercises the success path and the overload rejection path, but not the partial failure scenario. If codec creation leaves objects in an inconsistent state, subsequent calls to `onData()` may behave unpredictably.\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `CodecCreationPartialFailureRecovery`\n  - Setup: Mock `config_->createCodec()` to succeed on first call partially (allocate internal buffers), then fail on re-entry\n  - Action: Call `onData()` with valid HTTP data\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify connection is properly cleaned up (no dangling codec pointers)\n    - Verify stats are correctly incremented (codec_creation_error counter)\n    - Verify subsequent `onData()` calls don't crash or leak resources\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  A partially initialized codec could lead to memory leaks, nullptr dereferences, or double-free bugs. This is especially critical in production systems handling thousands of concurrent connections under load.\n\n### Gap 2: Premature Reset Detection Heuristic Edge Cases\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 702-749 (function `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()`)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n- **Description**:\n  The premature reset detection uses a heuristic formula (`number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2`) to decide whether to drain the connection (lines 731, 735). The test suite does not cover:\n  - Boundary conditions where `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2` exactly equals the limit\n  - Overflow scenarios when `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` is very large (near UINT64_MAX)\n  - Rapid successive premature resets in a single dispatch cycle\n  - Interaction with the `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag preventing recursion (the flag itself is well-tested, but the boundary conditions triggering it are not)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `PrematureResetEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Set `number_premature_stream_resets_` = 250 and `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` = 500 (exactly at 2x boundary). Verify connection is drained.\n  - Test Case 2: Set `number_premature_stream_resets_` = 249 and `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` = 500 (just below boundary). Verify connection is NOT drained.\n  - Test Case 3: Create 1000 streams, reset 60% prematurely in rapid succession. Verify GOAWAY is sent exactly once, not multiple times.\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` is incremented exactly once\n    - Verify `doConnectionClose()` is called exactly once\n    - Verify subsequent `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` calls are no-ops due to `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` flag\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Premature resets often indicate a client or network problem. Failing to detect and isolate such connections could allow malicious clients to degrade service for other users. Conversely, false positives (draining connections that shouldn't be drained) could reduce availability.\n\n### Gap 3: Header Validation and Transformation Error Path Coverage\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 1195-1254 (function `validateHeaders()` including transformation)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The header validation logic handles multiple failure scenarios:\n  - Path normalization redirects (line 1210-1227: sets Location header, responds with 307)\n  - gRPC special handling (line 1228-1230: uses grpc_status instead of response_code)\n  - HTTP/2 underscore validation special case (line 1238-1247: resets stream instead of sending response)\n\n  Current tests focus on the happy path and basic validation failure. The test suite does NOT cover:\n  - Interaction between multiple validation failures (e.g., underscore violation AND path normalization redirect)\n  - gRPC stream responses to header validation failures (does gRPC-specific error handling work correctly?)\n  - Edge case where `response_encoder_->streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` returns different values per stream\n  - Validation of trailers (separate function `validateTrailers()` at lines 1256-1300) with edge cases like trailers containing underscores\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `HeaderValidationEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Send request with invalid underscore AND attempt path normalization. Verify HTTP/2 codec resets stream (not sending 400).\n  - Test Case 2: Send gRPC request with invalid Content-Type header. Verify response code is Internal (grpc_status) not BadRequest.\n  - Test Case 3: Send trailers with underscores on HTTP/1. Verify local reply is sent (not stream reset).\n  - Test Case 4: Send trailers with invalid encoding on HTTP/2. Verify codec error is NOT triggered (per line 1295 check).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify correct response codes (307, 400, or stream reset) based on protocol and error type\n    - Verify gRPC status codes are set when appropriate\n    - Verify stats are correct (`downstream_rq_failed_path_normalization_`, `downstream_rq_redirected_with_normalized_path_`)\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Invalid header handling is the first line of defense against protocol violations. Bugs here could allow malformed requests to bypass validation, reach upstream services, or cause protocol state corruption in HTTP/2 and HTTP/3.\n\n### Gap 4: Filter Chain Continuation with 1xx Headers Interaction\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/filter_manager.cc\n- **Lines**: 61-146 (function `ActiveStreamFilterBase::commonContinue()`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The filter continuation logic is complex when 1xx (informational) headers are involved. Lines 88-96 show:\n  ```cpp\n  if (has1xxHeaders()) {\n    continued_1xx_headers_ = true;\n    do1xxHeaders();\n    if (!parent_.filter_manager_callbacks_.responseHeaders()) {\n      return;  // Early exit if final headers not yet arrived\n    }\n  }\n  ```\n\n  Current tests verify basic 1xx header flow, but NOT:\n  - What happens if a filter modifies `continued_1xx_headers_` state during `do1xxHeaders()` (should be impossible but not explicitly asserted)\n  - If `has1xxHeaders()` returns true but `do1xxHeaders()` somehow fails to actually send them\n  - If both `has1xxHeaders()` and `hasTrailers()` return true - which takes priority in continuation order?\n  - If response headers arrive WHILE `do1xxHeaders()` is executing (re-entrancy with mixed state)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `FilterContinuation1xxInteraction`\n  - Test Case 1: Filter returns StopAllBuffer on first headers, then continues after 1xx headers received. Verify `do1xxHeaders()` is called before `doHeaders()`.\n  - Test Case 2: Multiple 1xx headers received (100 Continue, then 103 Early Hints). Verify both are processed, or verify behavior is well-defined for multiple 1xx headers.\n  - Test Case 3: 1xx headers received, then trailers received before continuation. Verify continuation order is: 1xx → headers → trailers.\n  - Test Case 4: Filter returns `StopAllWatermark`, then watermark is resolved while 1xx headers are pending. Verify 1xx headers are still processed.\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `do1xxHeaders()` and `doHeaders()` are called in correct order\n    - Verify `doTrailers()` is called after headers, not before\n    - Verify stream state machine is consistent (no double-processing of headers)\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  HTTP/1.1 continues (100 Continue) and HTTP/1.1 early hints (103 Early Hints) require precise timing. Filter bugs could cause timeouts (client waits for 100 Continue), connection hangs, or protocol violations (sending headers twice).\n\n### Gap 5: HTTP/1 Soft Drain on Max Connection Duration\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 769-788 (function `onConnectionDurationTimeout()`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  When `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` is enabled for HTTP/1, the code avoids full drain sequence and instead sets `soft_drain_http1_ = true` (line 783). This is an optimization to avoid expensive GOAWAY for HTTP/1. However, the test suite does not cover:\n  - What happens if a NEW stream is created AFTER soft_drain_http1_ is set (line 437-441 in newStream() marks stream to drain on completion)\n  - Interaction between soft_drain and other drain sequences (what if startDrainSequence() was already called?)\n  - Verify that `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` is decremented exactly once in destructor (line 238)\n  - Edge case: soft_drain_http1_ set, then immediately another timeout fires (stream timeout, connection close timeout)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `HTTP1SoftDrainEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Set `http1SafeMaxConnectionDuration()` = true, max_connection_duration = 100ms. Create a stream that takes longer than 100ms to complete. Verify `soft_drain_http1_` is set, stream still completes, then connection closes gracefully.\n  - Test Case 2: Multiple streams exist, max connection duration timeout fires. Verify all streams are allowed to complete (not forcibly closed like in full drain).\n  - Test Case 3: Soft drain timeout, then client sends another request. Verify request is accepted and processed (no immediate GOAWAY).\n  - Test Case 4: Soft drain flag set, then `onDrainTimeout()` is called. Verify GOAWAY is still sent (drain sequence takes precedence).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `soft_drain_http1_` flag is set (not starting full drain sequence)\n    - Verify `stats_.named_.downstream_cx_http1_soft_drain_` is incremented and later decremented\n    - Verify connection doesn't close until all streams complete\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Soft drain is a performance optimization to avoid expensive GOAWAY messages in HTTP/1. Bugs could cause unnecessary connection closures (impacting client performance) or violate the optimization contract (sending expensive GOAWAY anyway).\n\n### Gap 6: Stream End with Concurrent Trailers and End-Stream Events\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 259-310 (function `doEndStream()`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  The `doEndStream()` function handles a complex scenario: deciding whether to reset the stream or let it complete naturally. Lines 271-273 check:\n  ```cpp\n  if (stream.response_encoder_ != nullptr &&\n      (!stream.filter_manager_.hasLastDownstreamByteReceived() ||\n       !stream.state_.codec_saw_local_complete_))\n  ```\n\n  The test suite covers basic stream end, but NOT:\n  - Stream end when trailers are present (hasTrailers() = true) but response_encoder is still attached\n  - The interaction between `hasLastDownstreamByteReceived()` and trailers (trailers should mark this as true, but are they processed before doEndStream()?)\n  - Call to `recreateStream()` which nulls out response_encoder (line 268 comment) - what if recreateStream() fails?\n  - Edge case where `state_.codec_saw_local_complete_` is true but request data is still being transmitted upstream\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `StreamEndWithTrailersEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Request with headers + trailers, filter takes a long time to process. Verify trailers are recorded via `maybeRecordLastByteReceived()` before stream end.\n  - Test Case 2: Response sent (marking local complete), then trailers arrive from downstream. Verify stream is reset (not allowed per HTTP semantics).\n  - Test Case 3: `recreateStream()` is called internally. Verify `response_encoder_` is properly nulled and stream is not reset.\n  - Test Case 4: Stream has trailers, doEndStream() is called, then filter injects more trailers. Verify order of operations (stream doesn't actually end mid-trailer-injection).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify trailers are properly recorded with timing information\n    - Verify stream reset happens when appropriate (incomplete requests)\n    - Verify response_encoder is not accessed after recreateStream()\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Stream end logic is critical for proper request lifecycle. Bugs could cause premature stream resets (losing data), protocol violations (sending response twice), or memory safety issues (use-after-free).\n\n### Gap 7: Request Header Timeout Firing During Filter Processing\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 1335-1338 (request_header_timer setup and disabling in decodeHeaders)\n- **Risk**: LOW\n- **Description**:\n  Request header timeout is set when a stream is created and disabled when headers are decoded (line 1336). However, the test suite does not cover:\n  - What if header timeout fires WHILE `decodeHeaders()` is executing? (Re-entrancy: timeout callback fires during header processing)\n  - What if timeout fires after headers received but before timeout is disabled? (Race condition)\n  - What if multiple streams are created and only some get their header timeouts fire?\n  - Interaction with stream-idle-timeout: which takes precedence if both fire simultaneously?\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `RequestHeaderTimeoutEdgeCases`\n  - Test Case 1: Create stream, immediately fire request_header_timer. Verify stream is reset (or connection is closed) before headers are processed.\n  - Test Case 2: Create stream, start sending headers but very slowly. Fire timeout during header transmission. Verify timeout is honored (not waiting for full headers).\n  - Test Case 3: Create two streams. Timeout fires on first stream while second stream is being created. Verify only first stream is affected.\n  - Test Case 4: Request headers timeout = 100ms, stream idle timeout = 200ms. Timeout fires at 100ms. Verify header timeout is enforced (not waiting for stream idle timeout).\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify `stats_.named_.downstream_rq_pending_header_timeout_` is incremented\n    - Verify connection is either closed or stream is reset\n    - Verify no leaked resources (timers, streams)\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Header timeouts protect against slowloris attacks. Missing edge case handling could allow attacks to slip through or cause false positives (legitimate slow clients).\n\n### Gap 8: Header Map Lazy-to-Eager Conversion Boundary Conditions\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 56-68 (function `HeaderMapImpl::HeaderList::maybeMakeMap()`)\n- **Risk**: LOW\n- **Description**:\n  The header map uses a lazy-map optimization. Headers are stored in a linked list until 3 headers are present, then a map is created (line 26: `kMinHeadersForLazyMap = 3`). The test suite covers basic operations, but NOT:\n  - Creating exactly 3 headers then immediately looking up a header (boundary condition triggering lazy map creation)\n  - Removing headers back to 2, then adding one more (does lazy map stay, or is it destroyed?)\n  - Performance characteristics: does the lazy map handle worst-case lookups efficiently?\n  - Header removal during map iteration (concurrent modification)\n\n- **Proposed Test**: `HeaderMapLazyToEagerBoundary`\n  - Test Case 1: Add 2 headers, verify lazy_map is empty. Add 3rd header, verify lazy_map is created and contains all 3.\n  - Test Case 2: Add 3 headers (lazy map created), remove 1 header. Verify lazy map is correctly updated (not left in inconsistent state).\n  - Test Case 3: Add 5 headers (lazy map created), look up each via key. Verify all are found (lazy map is correct).\n  - Test Case 4: Add 10 custom headers with same name. Verify lazy map stores list of values correctly.\n  - Assertions:\n    - Verify lazy_map_.empty() == true when headers.size() < 3\n    - Verify lazy_map_.empty() == false when headers.size() >= 3 (after first lazy_map trigger)\n    - Verify all lookups return correct values, whether lazy map is used or not\n\n- **Why It Matters**:\n  Header map is used in the hot path for every HTTP request. Performance bugs or correctness issues here could cause O(n) behavior when O(log n) is expected, leading to CPU overhead or incorrect header values being returned.\n\n### Gap 9: Codec Error Propagation to Active Streams\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 463-482 (functions `handleCodecError()` and `handleCodecOverloadError()`)\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Description**:\n  When a codec error occurs (e.g., invalid frame format, protocol violation), `handleCodecError()` is called (line 529, 531, etc.). Bad actors could exploit gaps to cause denial of service or connection pool exhaustion.\n\n### Gap 10: Stream Creation with Buffer Account Memory Pressure\n\n- **File**: source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc\n- **Lines**: 409-421 (buffer account creation in `newStream()`)\n- **Risk**: LOW\n- **Description**:\n  When a new stream is created, a buffer account is created for watermark tracking (lines 415-417).
